nd gn bk">Writer: Ilan Duhin</p><h2 id="ee1a" class="ne nf gu bf ng nh ni dy nj nk nl ea nm mr nn no np mv nq nr ns mz nt nu nv nw bk">Executive Summary:</h2><p id="e82d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj nx ml mm mn ny mp mq mr nz mt mu mv oa mx my mz ob nb nc nd gn bk">Petya is a family of encrypting malware that targets OS of windows to infect MBR (master boot record) to execute payload that encrypt a hard drive’s file system table.</p><p id="731a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">Petya spread over the network by using the exploit MS17–010 Vulnerability known as <strong class="mi gv">EternalBlue.</strong> It also spreads by stealing <strong class="mi gv">user names &amp; passwords</strong> and spreading across network shares.</p><blockquote class="oc od oe"><p id="a8d9" class="mg mh of mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk"><strong class="mi gv">Static Analysis:</strong></p></blockquote><p id="0ef9" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">when I opened the ransomware in <strong class="mi gv">IDA</strong>, it started at the 10007D39 address with the function DLLEntryPoint, so although the file extension is .exe, I guess it is actually DLL.</p><figure mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">The interesting libraries I focus on them is:</p><p id="45ba" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">· <strong class="mi gv">Crypt32.dll</strong> — will use possibly crypto functions.</p><p id="258a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">· <strong class="mi gv">Advapi32.dll</strong> — probably will be responsible for restarting the OS system (I guess because the ransomware wants to reboot the machine after she encrypts all files).</p><p id="d31a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">· <strong class="mi gv">Shlwapi.dll</strong> — function that works for strings &amp; filesystems paths.</p><p id="72d7" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">· <strong class="mi gv">Ws2_32.dll</strong> — it contains windows sockets api, I guess for setting up some sockets.</p><p id="910a" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">Another way to find interesting things about ransomware is by reading her string. To do this I use <strong class="mi gv">BinText.</strong></p><p id="4445" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">The strings bk">IDA:</p><p id="780d" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu mv mw mx my mz na nb nc nd gn bk">- One of the thing I am doing when I dropped the file into (Basically it’s a table that shows us memory location of every symbol — API calls of the malware code)</p><p id="e46f" class="pw-post-body-paragraph mg mh gu mi b mj mk ml mm mn mo mp mq mr ms mt mu
